queries and returns query responses. It handles queries to single or mixed datasources, as well as expressions.\n   101→func (s *ServiceImpl) queryData(ctx context.Context, user identity.Requester, skipDSCache bool, reqDTO dtos.MetricRequest, supportLocaltimeRange bool) (*backend.QueryDataResponse, error) {\n   102→\tfromAlert := false\n   103→\tfor header, val := range s.headers {\n   104→\t\tif header == models.FromAlertHeaderName && val == \"true\" {\n   105→\t\t\tfromAlert = true\n   106→\t\t}\n   107→\t}\n   108→\t// Parse the request into parsed queries grouped by datasource uid\n   109→\tparsedReq, err := s.parseMetricRequest(ctx, user, skipDSCache, reqDTO, supportLocaltimeRange)\n   110→\tif err != nil {\n   111→\t\treturn nil, err\n   112→\t}\n   113→\n   114→\t// If there are expressions, handle them and return\n   115→\tif parsedReq.hasExpression || fromAlert {\n   116→\t\treturn s.handleExpressions(ctx, user, parsedReq)\n   117→\t}\n   118→\t// If there is only one datasource, query it and return\n   119→\tif len(parsedReq.parsedQueries) == 1 {\n   120→\t\treturn s.handleQuerySingleDatasource(ctx, user, parsedReq)\n   121→\t}\n   122→\t// If there are multiple datasources, handle their queries concurrently and return the aggregate result\n   123→\treturn s.executeConcurrentQueries(ctx, user, skipDSCache, reqDTO, parsedReq.parsedQueries)\n   124→}\n   125→\n   126→func (s *ServiceImpl) QueryData(ctx context.Context, user identity.Requester, skipDSCache bool, reqDTO dtos.MetricRequest) (*backend.QueryDataResponse, error) {\n   127→\treturn s.queryData(ctx, user, skipDSCache, reqDTO, false)\n   128→}\n   129→\n   130→func (s *ServiceImpl) QueryDataNew(ctx context.Context, user identity.Requester, skipDSCache bool, reqDTO dtos.MetricRequest) (*backend.QueryDataResponse, error) {\n   131→\treturn s.queryData(ctx, user, skipDSCache, reqDTO, true)\n   132→}\n   133→\n   134→// splitResponse contains the results of a concurrent data source query - %s\", s.cfg.UserFacingDefaultError)\n   157→\t\t\t}\n   158→\t\t\t// Due to the panic, there is no valid response for any query for this datasource. Append an error for each one.\n   159→\t\t\trchan <- buildErrorResponses(err, queries)\n   160→\t\t}\n   161→\t}\n   162→\n   163→\t// Query each datasource concurrently\n   164→\tfor _, queries := range queriesbyDs {\n   165→\t\trawQueries := make([]*simplejson.Json, len(queries))\n   166→\t\tfor i := 0; These queries should all belong to the same datasource.\n   217→func buildErrorResponses(err error, queries []*simplejson.Json) splitResponse {\n   218→\ter := backend.Responses{}\n   219→\tfor _, getDataSourceFromQuery(ctx context.Context, user identity.Requester, skipDSCache bool, query *simplejson.Json, history map[string]*datasources.DataSource) (*datasources.DataSource, error) {\n   430→\tvar err error\n   431→\tuid := query.Get(\"datasource\").Get(\"uid\").MustString()\n   432→\n   433→\t// before 8.3 special types could be sent as datasource (expr)\n   434→\tif uid == \"\" {\n (*ServiceImpl)(nil)\n\ntype ServiceImpl struct {\n\tcfg                        *setting.Cfg\n\tdataSourceCache            datasources.CacheService\n\texpressionService It handles queries to single or mixed datasources, as well as expressions.\nfunc (s *ServiceImpl) queryData(ctx context.Context, user identity.Requester, skipDSCache bool, reqDTO dtos.MetricRequest, supportLocaltimeRange bool) (*backend.QueryDataResponse, error) {\n\tfromAlert := false\n\tfor header, val := range s.headers {\n\t\tif header == models.FromAlertHeaderName && val == \"true\" {\n\t\t\tfromAlert = true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\t// Parse the request into parsed queries grouped by datasource uid\n\tparsedReq, err := s.parseMetricRequest(ctx, user, skipDSCache, reqDTO, supportLocaltimeRange)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\t// If there are expressions, handle them and return\n\tif parsedReq.hasExpression || fromAlert {\n\t\treturn s.handleExpressions(ctx, user, parsedReq)\n\t}\n\t// If there is only one datasource, query it and return\n\tif len(parsedReq.parsedQueries) == 1 {\n\t\treturn s.handleQuerySingleDatasource(ctx, user, parsedReq)\n\t}\n\t// If there are multiple datasources, handle their queries concurrently and return the aggregate result\n\treturn s.executeConcurrentQueries(ctx, user, skipDSCache, reqDTO, parsedReq.parsedQueries)\n}\n\nfunc (s *ServiceImpl) QueryData(ctx context.Context, user identity.Requester, skipDSCache bool, reqDTO dtos.MetricRequest) (*backend.QueryDataResponse, error) {\n\treturn s.queryData(ctx, user, skipDSCache, reqDTO, false)\n}\n\nfunc (s *ServiceImpl) QueryDataNew(ctx context.Context, user identity.Requester, skipDSCache bool, reqDTO dtos.MetricRequest) (*backend.QueryDataResponse, error) {\n\treturn s.queryData(ctx, user, skipDSCache, reqDTO, true)\n}\n\n// splitResponse contains the results of a concurrent data source query - %s\", s.cfg.UserFacingDefaultError)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t// Due to the panic, there is no valid response for any query for this datasource. Append an error for each one.\n\t\t\trchan <- buildErrorResponses(err, queries)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Query each datasource concurrently\n\tfor _, queries := range queriesbyDs {\n\t\trawQueries := make([]*simplejson.Json, len(queries))\n\t\tfor i := 0; i < len(queries); i++ {\n\t\t\trawQueries[i] = queries[i].rawQuery\n\t\t}\n\t\tg.Go(func() error {\n\t\t\tsubDTO := reqDTO.CloneWithQueries(rawQueries)\n\t\t\t// Handle panics in the datasource qery\n\t\t\tdefer recoveryFn(subDTO.Queries)\n\n\t\t\tctxCopy := contexthandler.CopyWithReqContext(ctx)\n\t\t\tsubResp, err := s.QueryData(ctxCopy, user, skipDSCache, subDTO)\n\t\t\tif err == nil {\n\t\t\t\treqCtx, header := contexthandler.FromContext(ctxCopy), http.Header{}\n\t\t\t\tif reqCtx != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\theader = reqCtx.Resp.Header()\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\trchan <- splitResponse{subResp.Responses, header}\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// If there was an error, return an error response for each query for this datasource\n\t\t\t\trchan <- buildErrorResponses(err, subDTO.Queries)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\n\tif err := g.Wait(); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\tclose(rchan)\n\tresp := backend.NewQueryDataResponse()\n\treqCtx := contexthandler.FromContext(ctx)\n\tfor result := range rchan {\n\t\tfor refId, dataResponse := range result.responses {\n\t\t\tresp.Responses[refId] = dataResponse\n\t\t}\n\t\tif reqCtx != nil {\n\t\t\tfor k, v := range result.header {\n\t\t\t\tfor _, val := range v {\n\t\t\t\t\tif !slices.Contains(reqCtx.Resp.Header().Values(k), val) {\n\t\t\t\t\t\treqCtx.Resp.Header().Add(k, val)\n\t\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\t\ts.log.Warn(\"skipped duplicate response header\", \"header\", k, \"value\", val)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn resp, nil\n}\n\n// buildErrorResponses applies the provided error to each query response in the list. 312→\t\t\t}\n   313→\t\t}\n   314→\t}\n   315→}\n   316→\n   317→// Hop-by-hop headers. These are the headers defined by the\n   320→// obsoleted RFC 2616 (section 13.5.1) and are used for backward\n   321→// compatibility.\n   322→//\n   323→// Copied from https://github.com/golang/go/blob/dc04f3ba1f25313bc9c97e728620206c235db9ee/src/net/http/httputil/reverseproxy.go#L171-L186\n   324→var hopHeaders = []string{\n   325→\t\"Connection\",\n   326→\t\"Proxy-Connection\", // non-standard but still sent by libcurl and rejected by e.g. google\n   327→\t\"Keep-Alive\",\n   328→\t\"Proxy-Authenticate\",\n   329→\t\"Proxy-Authorization\",\n   330→\t\"Te\",      // canonicalized version of \"TE\"\n   331→\t\"Trailer\", // not Trailers per URL above; https://www.rfc-editor.org/errata_search.php?eid=4522\n   332→\t\"Transfer-Encoding\",\n   333→\t\"Upgrade\",\n   334→\t\"User-Agent\",\n   335→}\n   336→\n   337→// removeHopByHopHeaders removes hop-by-hop headers. Especially\n   338→// important is \"Connection\" because we want a persistent\n   339→// connection, regardless of what the client sent to us.\n   340→//\n   341→// Based on https://github.com/golang/go/blob/dc04f3ba1f25313bc9c97e728620206c235db9ee/src/net/http/httputil/reverseproxy.go#L276-L281\n   342→func removeHopByHopHeaders(h map[string][]string) {\n   343→\tfor _, hh := range hopHeaders {\n   344→\t\tfor k := range h {\n   345→\t\t\tif hh == textproto.CanonicalMIMEHeaderKey(k) {\n   346→\t\t\t\tdelete(h, k)\n   347→\t\t\t\tbreak\n   348→\t\t\t}\n   349→\t\t}\n   350→\t}\n   351→}\n   352→\n   353→func removeNonAllowedHeaders(h map[string][]string) {\n   354→\tfor k := range h {\n   355→\t\tif textproto.CanonicalMIMEHeaderKey(k) == setCookieHeaderName {\n   356→\t\t\tdelete(h, k)\n   357→\t\t}\n   358→\t}\n   359→}\n   360→\n   361→// ensureContentTypeHeader makes sure a content type always is returned in response.\n   362→func ensureContentTypeHeader(res *backend.CallResourceResponse) {\n   363→\tif res == nil {\n   364→\t\treturn\n   365→\t}\n   366→\n   367→\tvar hasContentType bool\n   368→\tfor k := range res.Headers {\n   369→\t\tif textproto.CanonicalMIMEHeaderKey(k) == contentTypeHeaderName {\n   370→\t\t\thasContentType = true\n   371→\t\t\tbreak\n   372→\t\t}\n   373→\t}\n   374→\n   375→\tif !hasContentType && res.Status != http.StatusNoContent {\n   376→\t\tres.Headers[contentTypeHeaderName] = []string{defaultContentType}\n   377→\t}\n   378→}\n   379→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
